<div id="review_1259302386" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1259302386" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588746288p2/10326608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1259302386?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326608-lindsay?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326608-lindsay?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1259302386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2065175587538596000">Part of the Pratchett reread with the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2019.<br/><br/>This entry in the Watch series sees Vimes and Vetinari dealing with the sudden reappearance of the of the lost island of Leshp and the political consequences. In particular, a brewing war with neighboring Klatch. Vimes, as ever, is struggling with the fast-growing Watch and the responsibilities that creates for a very hands-on Watch Commander with everything suffering, including sleep and his relationship with Sybil.<br/><br/>While th</span>
  <span id="freeText2065175587538596000" style="display:none">Part of the Pratchett reread with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2019.<br /><br />This entry in the Watch series sees Vimes and Vetinari dealing with the sudden reappearance of the of the lost island of Leshp and the political consequences. In particular, a brewing war with neighboring Klatch. Vimes, as ever, is struggling with the fast-growing Watch and the responsibilities that creates for a very hands-on Watch Commander with everything suffering, including sleep and his relationship with Sybil.<br /><br />While the Watch and Vimes are front and center here, this book is unusual in that it shows Lord Vetinari taking a direct hand in events and he makes an excellent major character for a change. This is also Pratchett's platform for having a conversation about racism and nationalism, particularly from his supremely humanist mindset. It's wryly funny at most points, only occasionally venturing into hilarity and tragedy as needed with Pratchett's deft touch for both. It's not the best Watch book, but it continues the trajectory of the Watch series in getting better as they go. Highly recommended (as most of the Discworld books are).</span>
  <a data-text-id="2065175587538596000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer502921207315960427">I FOUND COMMANDER VIMES IN A CHARITY SHOP *happy dance* - you must know how rare this is. Yoink, HAVING THAT.<br/><br/>------------<br/><br/>From 2012:<br/><br/>It's not very often in the next few months that I'm going to get to read a whole book in a day, so I thought, in for a penny, in for a pound, took a Sunday off and settled down with Commander Vimes and a bar of Dairy Milk.<br/><br/>It was a good choice. Of course it was. I've been recommended 'Jingo' several times, and it's perfectly obvious why: it's exactly my kind of thing.</span>
  <span id="freeText502921207315960427" style="display:none">I FOUND COMMANDER VIMES IN A CHARITY SHOP *happy dance* - you must know how rare this is. Yoink, HAVING THAT.<br /><br />------------<br /><br />From 2012:<br /><br />It's not very often in the next few months that I'm going to get to read a whole book in a day, so I thought, in for a penny, in for a pound, took a Sunday off and settled down with Commander Vimes and a bar of Dairy Milk.<br /><br />It was a good choice. Of course it was. I've been recommended 'Jingo' several times, and it's perfectly obvious why: it's exactly my kind of thing. A lot of page time is spent on my favourite supporting cast (Vetinari, Carrot, Angua) and Lady Sybil gets a good few pages of being wonderful as well. Including one where she's haphazardly knitting. If I were a more sentimental sort, I'd tell you know that we'd TOTALLY be best friends. As it is, I'm too busy giggling in glee at Carrot's myriad organisation of football matches.<br /><br />There seems to be a bit of a theme going on in my reading of late: a lot of it seems to have a very strong pacifist message. Vimes is right up there with Atticus Finch in terms of really shiny upholders of the law, and in 'Jingo' the law-abiding, but also strongly pacifist, message is possibly the strongest I've ever seen it in a Pratchett book.<br /><br />Anyway, I loved it. It was a bit confusing at times - I still didn't completely get the whole business about 71 hours - hence four stars instead of five. However, I think that's a long Sunday afternoon well spent.</span>
  <a data-text-id="502921207315960427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1836431075" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1836431075" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1836431075?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1836431075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer635157053635465184"><i>Jingo</i> is the fourth book in the <i>City Watch</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>. When I first started this subseries, I didn’t think I was going to like it very much. It’s grown on me, though, and I think it’s now my second favorite after the <i>Witches</i> subseries. <br/><br/>In this book, a disagreement between fishermen in the middle of the sea between Ankh-Morpork and Klatch triggers buried resentments and prejudices among citizens of both places until it appears that war is inevitable. As is common with this subseries, </span>
  <span id="freeText635157053635465184" style="display:none"><i>Jingo</i> is the fourth book in the <i>City Watch</i> subseries of <i>Discworld</i>. When I first started this subseries, I didn’t think I was going to like it very much. It’s grown on me, though, and I think it’s now my second favorite after the <i>Witches</i> subseries. <br /><br />In this book, a disagreement between fishermen in the middle of the sea between Ankh-Morpork and Klatch triggers buried resentments and prejudices among citizens of both places until it appears that war is inevitable. As is common with this subseries, there was a little bit of a mystery involved, and that helped keep the story more interesting. <br /><br />Pratchett often uses humor to impart some sort of a message, and I thought this book was one of the better examples of that. He used humor to point out the ridiculousness of how people tend to divide themselves into “us” and “them” and vilify the “them”, assuming the worst about their intentions and beliefs. There were a lot of very funny moments, and yet those ridiculously funny things weren’t so terribly far from the behavior of real people in our world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="635157053635465184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9582467768657395352">I don't think I've ever laughed so much because of a book as I have with this one. Terry Pratchett is a genius of comedic yet poignant writing.   <span id="freeText9582467768657395352" style="display:none">I don't think I've ever laughed so much because of a book as I have with this one. Terry Pratchett is a genius of comedic yet poignant writing. Which makes me that much sadder that he passed away.<br /><br />These books always start off slowly, with one common theme driving a narrative and an important issue and looking it through a ridiculous/comedic glasses in this one it's racism, xenophobia, and overt nationalism. <br /><br />I would have never thought that the pairing Vetinari, Nobby, and Colon would ever happen or work, but holy shit, so much gold. I could barely handle Nobby as Beti.<br /><br />Vimes and Carrot also continue to be national treasures. I do wish we'd take more focus on Angua, Cheri and Sybil. Hopefully, we'll get more of them, and maybe even have them interact in the next one.</span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=racism">racism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=quotable">quotable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=part_of_a_series">part_of_a_series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=politics">politics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1313943620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11194118929442173001">Ankh Morpork and Klatch have been at peace for a long time now. Klatchians would even send their sons to the prestigious Assassin's Guild Academy, and Ankh Morporkans (sp??) would happily lend money to neighbours. And yet, when a mysterious island emerges from the sea all bets are off. Both sides are set to claim the island of Leshp as their own.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456042646i/18182431._SX540_.jpg' alt='Ancient ruins on a mysterious island' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>There is an attempt at a diplomatic solution, when Prince Khufurah visits Ankh Morpork to talk with the Patrician. Nevertheless, things end badly for bo</span>
  <span id="freeText11194118929442173001" style="display:none">Ankh Morpork and Klatch have been at peace for a long time now. Klatchians would even send their sons to the prestigious Assassin's Guild Academy, and Ankh Morporkans (sp??) would happily lend money to neighbours. And yet, when a mysterious island emerges from the sea all bets are off. Both sides are set to claim the island of Leshp as their own.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456042646i/18182431._SX540_.jpg" alt="Ancient ruins on a mysterious island" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There is an attempt at a diplomatic solution, when Prince Khufurah visits Ankh Morpork to talk with the Patrician. Nevertheless, things end badly for both parties, after the Prince disappears amid the chaos of a flaming embassy. With no other alternatives, Ankh Morpork and Klatch are going to war. In the end, this shouldn't be a difficult endeavor, after all Klatch is very much indebted to the Ankh Morpork. On the other hand, the latter doesn't exactly have an army to speak of...<br><br><a href="http://k-cervantes.tumblr.com/post/102587751635/jingo-or-the-one-where-everyone-is-a-badass" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456042646i/18182432._SY540_.jpg" width="400" alt="Illustration of 71-hour Ahmed" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Illustrated by <a href="http://k-cervantes.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Karla Cervantes</a><br><br>Based on the 2-3 most popular reviews here, I wasn't expecting much from this installment of the City Watches adventures. So the fact that I ended up enjoying it so much, was a rather welcome surprise. Most importantly however, I have finally found a liking for Commander Vimes.<br><blockquote>
<br>It wasn’t spying, Commander Vimes told himself. Spying was when you crept around peeking in windows. It wasn’t spying when you had to stand back a bit so that you weren’t deafened.<br><br>Vimes’s approach to paperwork was not to touch it until someone was shouting, and then at least there would be someone to help him sort through the stacks.<br><br>“By the way, do you think anyone saw you up there?”<br>“I doubt it, sir. I was right in among the chimneys and the air vents.”<br>Vimes sighed. “Captain, I expect if you’d done it in a cellar at midnight his lordship would have said ‘Wasn’t it rather dark down there?’ next morning.”<br>
</blockquote><br><br>As far as Captain Carrot is concerned, he starred in plenty of hilarious scenes<br><br><blockquote>
<br>“Never mind, we did it! Now can we come out, please?” There was another sound behind the voice. It sounded like a low, continuous growl.<br>“I think you ought to be able to tell me what you stole,” said Carrot.<br>“Er…rings? Gold rings?”<br>“Sorry, no rings mentioned.”<br>“Pearl necklace? Yes, that’s what—”<br>“Getting warmer, but no.”<br>“Earrings?”<br>“Ooo, you’re so close,” said Carrot encouragingly.<br>“A crown, was it? Maybe a coronet?”<br>Carrot leaned down to the constable. “Says here a tiara, Reg, can we let—?” He stood up. “We’re prepared to accept ‘coronet.’ Well done!”<br><br>“What’s that little lump on Constable Flint’s head?”<br>“That’s Probationary Constable Buggy Swires, sir. He likes to get a good view.”<br>“He’s a gnome!”<br>“Well done, sir.”<br>“Another one of yours?”<br>“Ours, sir,” said Carrot, using his reproachful voice again. “Yes, sir. Attached to the Chitterling Street Station since last week, sir.”<br>
</blockquote><br><br>There were however, several exasperating moments between Angua and him. I totally sympathize with the girl.<br><br><blockquote>
<br>“Well, that’s a nice start to the day,” said Carrot.<br>“Thank you, yes, I wasn’t hurt,” said Angua.<br>“It makes it all seem worthwhile, somehow.”<br>“Just my hair messed up and another shirt ruined.”<br>“Well done.”<br>“Sometimes I might suspect that you don’t listen to anything I say,” said Angua.<br>“Glad to hear it,” said Carrot.<br><br>“Carrot, these disguises are meant for a potato.”<br>“Are they?”<br>“Look, they’re all on potatoes, see?”<br>“I thought that was just for display.”<br>“Carrot, it’s got ‘Mr. Spuddy Face’ on it.”<br>Behind his thick black moustache Carrot looked hurt and perplexed. “What does a potato want a disguise for?” he said.<br><br>The door opened a little way. “Ook?”<br>Carrot raised his horrible little round hat.<br>“Good evening, sir, I wonder if we could come in? It’s Watch business.”<br>“Ook eek ook?”<br>“Er…”<br>“What did he say?” said Angua.<br>“If you must know, he said, ‘My goodness me, a walking potato,’” said Carrot.<br>
</blockquote><br><br><strong>Score: 4/5 stars</strong><br><br>This was an especially memorable book, moreso given the current political situation in the Middle East. Basically, the dedication at the beginning of the book nailed it: <em>To all the fighters for peace</em><br><br>============================================<br>Other books featuring the City Watch:<br>Review of the 1st book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/848814884" rel="nofollow noopener">Guards!Guards!</a><br>Review of the 2nd book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1135571640" rel="nofollow noopener">Men at Arms</a><br>Review of the 3rd book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212951873" rel="nofollow noopener">Feet of Clay</a><br>Review of the 5th book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1319112593" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Elephant</a><br>Review of the 6th book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1319112623" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Watch</a><br>Review of the 7th book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/435878553" rel="nofollow noopener">Thud!</a><br>Review of the 8th book: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1319112687" rel="nofollow noopener">Snuff</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11194118929442173001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_404004529" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404004529" />
    <a title="Andree" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2863963-andree"><img alt="Andree" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/404004529?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andree" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andree" href="/user/show/2863963-andree">Andree</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/833436.Jingo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863963-andree?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863963-andree?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863963-andree?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer404004529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14113813741330774488">2016 Reread<br/><br/>Bumping this up a star the second time through. Even though I didn't remember a lot of this, despite it being one of my more recently read Discworld novels prior to the great 2016 TP read-through (fulfilling my earlier prediction that I wouldn't remember any of the details for any length of time).<br/><br/>Because this worked for me a lot better the second time around, perhaps because I'm now reading the Discworld in order. I have a better understanding of the dynamics of the Watch, and the dyn</span>
  <span id="freeText14113813741330774488" style="display:none">2016 Reread<br /><br />Bumping this up a star the second time through. Even though I didn't remember a lot of this, despite it being one of my more recently read Discworld novels prior to the great 2016 TP read-through (fulfilling my earlier prediction that I wouldn't remember any of the details for any length of time).<br /><br />Because this worked for me a lot better the second time around, perhaps because I'm now reading the Discworld in order. I have a better understanding of the dynamics of the Watch, and the dynamics between Vetinari and Vimes. After all, when I first read this one, I hadn't read either <i>Men at Arms</i> or Feet of Clay, and while you can read TP out of order, and still understand, the Watch, the Witches and the Death books are all serialized. (Rincewind technically is as well, but having started <i>The Last Continent</i> earlier today, I'm not convinced reading them in order would make much difference, except for maybe some of the scenes with the University wizards).<br /><br />Also bumping this up, because that last scene between Vetinari and Vimes in the aftermath of the war is a delight. Particularly having just read <i>Feet of Clay</i>. I also really enjoyed Vimes realizing that he was technically a knight and could, nay was required to, start up his own regiment. The scene where he announces that to the war-mongering Lord Rust made me smile. Vimes may be my favourite single Discworld character, if I had to pick one. I even enjoyed the Vetinari/Nobby/Colon dynamic a lot more this time around. Oh, and Vimes and 71 hour Ahmed, and Vimes and the Klatchians in general were great.<br /><br />Also, Lady Sibyl and Vimes continue to be one of my favourite things.<br /><br />Even the Angua plot hole felt like less of a plot hole this time around. I mean, it's sort of explainable, even if a few intermediate steps are missing in the text. But she's a werewolf, so clearly she could just find the Watch, even in the desert...<br /><br />Also really, really enjoyed <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the continued tradition of books in the Watch subseries ending with Carrot arresting something ridiculous. In this case, two armies. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I don't know. Part of it may be that I was reading this interspersed with a book club book that I'm struggling with and a cozy mystery that could have used an edit or two, and that sort of thing makes you realize how nice it is to read a book that just flows, and is enjoyable to read.<br /><br />Really enjoyed this. It's not perfect. There is still a bit of a lull in the middle, but I enjoyed it.<br /><br />---<br /><br />Enjoyed it a lot. Didn't love it.<br /><br />Thing is, I often enjoy Terry Pratchett. Particularly the books featuring either the Watch, or the witches. I like the books better when they're set in a familiar location.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the first half of this, with the watch sort of blundering around Ankh Morpok, with hilarious results. The Watch doing any kind of detective work is always fun!times. And I really enjoy Vimes and Sybil together.<br /><br />I also really enjoyed the last sixty pages or so. Vimes' butler is particularly great. And Carrot has grown on me a lot.<br /><br />This book made me laugh out loud a number of times.<br /><br />But there is a lull in the middle. In the desert, outside of the familiarity of the setting, things drag. And some of the odd combinations of people didn't quite work. (For example, I like Vetinari best when he's juxtaposed with Vimes, not Nobby.) Also, there's a definite plot whole related to Anguna.<br /><br />The other thing is, I suspect I won't rememmber more than a few details in a week. Maybe three. Because TP's books don't stay with me. I enjoy them while I read them, but they're often ephemeral. They're clever, extremely clever, and extremely entertaining, but sometimes they lack something in the core to centre around. There's a lack of character development, or something.<br /><br />(This is not always the case; when TP is at his best, the characters do drive the story, as opposed to the clever intellectual exercise cunningly dressed up in nonsense. Not that the intellectual exercise isn't fun, but in terms of a <i>story</i>, sometimes it's lacking.)<br /><br />So I can't give the book four stars, much as I enjoyed it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14113813741330774488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2944776093" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2944776093" />
    <a title="Alfred Haplo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34550725-alfred-haplo"><img alt="Alfred Haplo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599680519p2/34550725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2944776093?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alfred Haplo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alfred Haplo" href="/user/show/34550725-alfred-haplo">Alfred Haplo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780061059063" href="/book/show/400356.Jingo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34550725-alfred-haplo?shelf=1970-to-1999">1970-to-1999</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34550725-alfred-haplo?shelf=sf-fantasy-mytho">sf-fantasy-mytho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34550725-alfred-haplo?shelf=fun-haha">fun-haha</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2944776093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1044550663540225940">If only war is this funny. In <i>Jingo</i> *, humor and nationalism compete in a match-up, with laughter the clear winner. The victory, though, is a consolation for readers expecting more than the intent of war. The lead-in to a complex story is there - xenophobia, racism, jingoism - but for all the promise of anger and conflict and tension at the beginning, <i>Jingo</i> veers off to simpler, safer grounds. Occasionally, observers do rear their philosophical heads, those are <i>Jingo</i>’s finest moments, with Nobby</span>
  <span id="freeText1044550663540225940" style="display:none">If only war is this funny. In <i>Jingo</i> *, humor and nationalism compete in a match-up, with laughter the clear winner. The victory, though, is a consolation for readers expecting more than the intent of war. The lead-in to a complex story is there - xenophobia, racism, jingoism - but for all the promise of anger and conflict and tension at the beginning, <i>Jingo</i> veers off to simpler, safer grounds. Occasionally, observers do rear their philosophical heads, those are <i>Jingo</i>’s finest moments, with Nobby and Colon perfectly espousing how narrow-minded those heads are. <br /><br />Watchmen split off into mini self-directed missions that are largely undirected by the grand scheme of war. Certainly, they further endear my affection by sheer force of personality but more of the same disconnect between characters or staying in comfort zones would stagnate in future books. So, it’s really exciting when tweaked versions of favorite characters appear, for being familiar yet more... psychologically advanced. The new character of 71-hour Ahmed, whom I shall dub an honorary watchman, is such a refreshing breath of air (garlic mouth notwithstanding) for being unapologetically purposeful and menacing. Like a hardened, more intelligent version of his counterpart. Alas, they are but ships that pass in the night. <br /><br />What we have is twice the same character presented with different choices in two places simultaneously. No thanks to an annoying time device, Vimes-in-Klatch and Vimes-in-Ankh-Morpork face vastly different fates for his compatriots, though I wish the focus had been on the bloody side. <i>That’s</i> where the <i>real</i> war is, and where <i>real</i> victory can be won, and where <i>real</i> prejudices can be confronted. Where Pratchett could have taken <i>Jingo</i> to a whole other level instead of the voyage across the ocean to Klatch. Traipsing around desert enemy land and making funny with the locals do allow for more liveliness and comedy than policemen curbing racial riots on the homefront, but it feels disappointingly like a cop out for a plot that started out with an impending war. Perhaps a Middle Eastern-like diversity within the homeland and abroad was too much of a temptation for Pratchett to not play up the easy laughs on cultural ignorance and ethnic stereotypes. The effect, while humorous, feels tired. <br /><br />Perhaps Pratchett only meant to highlight the absurdity of pretext for war. That war is not solution, but a reaction to already existing internal warring interests. No man’s land is free for all when only squids swim in it, but a barren rock with smelly seaweed becomes sovereign land for all free man. When the tiny island of Leshp mysteriously surfaces in the Circle Sea midway between Ankh Morpork and Klatch, it provides the impetus for territorial clamor that starts and ends the same way - much ado about nothing. War is funny that way. <br /><br />Recommended for sub-series completion, but no loss skipped. <br /><br /><br />[* DiscWorld, Watch sub-series: <i>Guards! Guards!</i> (#8, #1), <i>Men At Arms</i> (#15, #2), <i>Feet of Clay</i> (#19, #3), <i>Jingo</i> (#21, #4) and others]</span>
  <a data-text-id="1044550663540225940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4900241557469360269">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText4900241557469360269" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4900241557469360269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
